<p><b>Sheffield Wednesday Football Club</b> is a professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, England. The team competes in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a>, the second tier of the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a>. Formed in 1867 as an offshoot of <a href="/wiki/The_Wednesday_Cricket_Club" title="The Wednesday Cricket Club">The Wednesday Cricket Club</a> (itself formed in 1820), they went by the name of the <b>Wednesday Football Club</b> until changing to their current name in 1929.
</p><p>Wednesday is one of the <a href="/wiki/Oldest_football_clubs" title="Oldest football clubs">oldest football clubs</a> in the world of any code, and the third-oldest professional association football club in England.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> In 1868 its team won the <a href="/wiki/Cromwell_Cup" title="Cromwell Cup">Cromwell Cup</a>, only the second tournament of its kind. They were founding members and inaugural champions of the <a href="/wiki/Football_Alliance" title="Football Alliance">Football Alliance</a> in 1889, before joining <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">The Football League</a> three years later. In 1992 they became founder members of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. The team has spent most of its league history in English football's top flight, but they have not played at that level since being relegated in 2000.
</p><p>The Owls, as they are nicknamed, have won four <a href="/wiki/English_football_champions" class="mw-redirect" title="English football champions">league titles</a>, three <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cups</a>, one <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> and one <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Community Shield</a>. Wednesday have also competed in <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> cup competitions on four occasions, reaching the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup" title="Inter-Cities Fairs Cup">Inter-Cities Fairs Cup</a> in 1963. In 1991 they defeated Manchester United 1-0 in the <a href="/wiki/1991_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1991 Football League Cup Final">Football League Cup Final</a> as a tier 2 team. As of 2019 they remain the last team outside the top flight to win one of English football's major trophies<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 19th century they played their matches at several stadiums around central Sheffield, most notabally <a href="/wiki/Olive_Grove" title="Olive Grove">Olive Grove</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>. Since 1899 the club has played all its home matches at <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough stadium</a>, a near-40,000 capacity stadium in the north-west Sheffield suburb of <a href="/wiki/Owlerton" title="Owlerton">Owlerton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="History of Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">History of Sheffield Wednesday F.C.</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C._seasons" title="List of Sheffield Wednesday F.C. seasons">List of Sheffield Wednesday F.C. seasons</a></div>
<h3><span id="Early_years_.281867.E2.80.931889.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_(1867–1889)">Early years (1867–1889)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg/220px-Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg/330px-Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg/440px-Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="688" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Darnall_cricket_ground.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A cricket match at Darnall in the 1820s, a ground laid out for <a href="/wiki/The_Wednesday_Cricket_Club" title="The Wednesday Cricket Club">The Wednesday Cricket Club</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Although no contemporary evidence has been found to support the claim, it is commonly believed that "The Wednesday Cricket Club" was formed in 1820.<sup id="cite_ref-Origins_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Origins-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, an 1842 article in <a href="/wiki/Bell%27s_Life_in_London" title="Bell&#39;s Life in London">Bell's Life</a> magazine states the club was founded as far back as 1816.<sup id="cite_ref-Origins_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Origins-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The club was so named because it was on Wednesdays that the founding members had their day off work. They were initially based at the <a href="/wiki/Darnall_New_Ground" title="Darnall New Ground">New Ground</a> in <a href="/wiki/Darnall" title="Darnall">Darnall</a>, and often went by the name of <i>Darnall Wednesday</i>, but also played at <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Sheffield" title="Hyde Park, Sheffield">Hyde Park</a>. In 1855 they were one of six clubs that helped build <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>, and held a wicket there for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-Origins_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Origins-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Famous players to have represented the cricket club include Harry Sampson, who scored 162 on ice in 1841, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Marsden" title="Tom Marsden">Tom Marsden</a>, who scored 227 for Sheffield &amp; Leicester vs Nottingham in 1826, and <a href="/wiki/George_Ulyett" title="George Ulyett">George Ulyett</a>, who represented the club in the <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_Australia_and_New_Zealand_in_1876%E2%80%9377" title="English cricket team in Australia and New Zealand in 1876–77">first ever international test match</a> before becoming one of only a select band of players who played for both sections of The Wednesday Club.
</p><p>On the evening of Wednesday 4 September 1867, a meeting was held at the <a href="/wiki/Adelphi_Hotel_(Sheffield)" title="Adelphi Hotel (Sheffield)">Adelphi Hotel</a> to establish whether there was interest among the club's members to form a football club to keep the team together and fit during the winter months. The proposal proved very popular, with over 60 members signing up for the new team on the first night. They played their first match against The Mechanics on 19 October the same year, winning by three goals and four '<a href="/wiki/Single_(football)" title="Single (football)">rouges</a>' to nil.<sup id="cite_ref-Sheffield_Football_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheffield_Football-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It soon became apparent that football would come to eclipse the cricketing side of the club in terms of popularity—the two sections went their separate ways in 1882 after a dispute over finances, and the cricket club ceased to exist in 1925. On 1 February 1868, Wednesday played their first competitive football match as they entered the <a href="/wiki/Cromwell_Cup" title="Cromwell Cup">Cromwell Cup</a>, a one-off four-team competition for newly formed clubs. A week after their semi-final, they went on to win the cup, beating the Garrick club in the final after extra time, the only goal being scored in diminishing light at <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>. This was the first recorded instance of a match being settled by a "<a href="/wiki/Golden_goal" title="Golden goal">golden goal</a>" although the term was not in use at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Cromwell_Cup_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cromwell_Cup-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A key figure during the formative years of the football club was <a href="/wiki/Charles_Clegg_(footballer)" title="Charles Clegg (footballer)">Charles Clegg</a>, who joined the Wednesday in 1867. His relationship with the club lasted for the rest of his life and eventually led to his becoming the club's chairman. He also became president and chairman of the <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a>, and was known as the "Napoleon of Football".<sup id="cite_ref-Statto_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statto-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Clegg played for <a href="/wiki/England_National_Football_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="England National Football Team">England</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1872_Scotland_v_England_football_match" title="1872 Scotland v England football match">first-ever international match</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_National_Football_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotland National Football Team">Scotland</a> in November 1872, thereby completing a unique double for the club, who could lay claim to having a player in the first international games of cricket and football.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TheWednesday1878.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/TheWednesday1878.jpg/220px-TheWednesday1878.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/TheWednesday1878.jpg/330px-TheWednesday1878.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/TheWednesday1878.jpg/440px-TheWednesday1878.jpg 2x" data-file-width="456" data-file-height="312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TheWednesday1878.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Wednesday team in 1878</div></div></div><p> In 1876 Wednesday acquired Scot <a href="/wiki/James_Lang_(footballer)" title="James Lang (footballer)">James Lang</a>. Although he was not employed by the club, he was given a job by a member of the Sheffield Wednesday board that had no formal duties. He is now acknowledged as the first professional football player in England.<sup id="cite_ref-In_the_Beginning_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_the_Beginning-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> With Lang in their team the football club became one of the strongest in the region, a reputation that was cemented when they won the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_%26_Hallamshire_Senior_Cup" title="Sheffield &amp; Hallamshire Senior Cup">Sheffield FA Challenge Cup</a> in 1877.
</p><p>In 1880 the club entered the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> for the first time, and they soon became one of the most respected sides in the country. But although they had had Lang on their books a decade earlier, the club officially remained staunchly amateur, and this stance almost cost the club its very existence.<sup id="cite_ref-Origins_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Origins-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> By the middle of the decade, Wednesday's best players were leaving in their droves to join clubs who would pay them, and in January 1887 they lost 0–16 against Halliwell with just 10 players in their team. An emergency meeting was held, and the board members finally agreed to pay its players.<sup id="cite_ref-Wednesday!_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wednesday!-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Professional_football_and_English_Champions_.281889.E2.80.931939.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_football_and_English_Champions_(1889–1939)">Professional football and English Champions (1889–1939)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg/250px-Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg/375px-Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg/500px-Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2540" data-file-height="1810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_wednesday_1896.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheffield Wednesday players posing with the FA Cup won in 1896</div></div></div>
<p>The move to professionalism took the club from Bramall Lane, which had taken a share of the ticket revenue, to the new <a href="/wiki/Olive_Grove" title="Olive Grove">Olive Grove</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Football_in_Sheffield_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Football_in_Sheffield-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 1889 the club became founder members of the <a href="/wiki/Football_Alliance" title="Football Alliance">Football Alliance</a>, of which they were the first champions in a season where they also reached the <a href="/wiki/1890_FA_Cup_Final" title="1890 FA Cup Final">1890 FA Cup Final</a>, losing 6–1 to <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kennington_Oval" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennington Oval">Kennington Oval</a>, London. Despite finishing the following season bottom of the Alliance, they were eventually elected to the expanded <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> in 1892. They won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> for the first time in <a href="/wiki/1896_FA_Cup_Final" title="1896 FA Cup Final">1896</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> 2–1 at <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_National_Sports_Centre" title="Crystal Palace National Sports Centre">Crystal Palace</a>.
</p><p>Owing to an expansion of the local railway lines, the club was told that they would have to find a new ground for the <a href="/wiki/1899%E2%80%931900_in_English_football" title="1899–1900 in English football">1899–1900 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wednesday!_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wednesday!-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> After a difficult search the club finally bought some land in the village of <a href="/wiki/Owlerton" title="Owlerton">Owlerton</a>, which at the time was several miles outside the Sheffield city boundaries. Construction of a new stadium (now known as <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough Stadium</a>) was completed within months and the club was secured for the next century. In a strong decade, Wednesday won the League in the <a href="/wiki/1902%E2%80%9303_in_English_football" title="1902–03 in English football">1902–03</a> and <a href="/wiki/1903%E2%80%9304_in_English_football" title="1903–04 in English football">1903–04</a> seasons and the FA Cup again in <a href="/wiki/1907_FA_Cup_Final" title="1907 FA Cup Final">1907</a>, beating <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> 2–1, again at Crystal Palace. When competitive football was suspended in 1915 because of the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_One" class="mw-redirect" title="World War One">World War One</a>, the club participated in several regionalised war leagues, until 1919, when normal service was resumed.
</p><p>They were relegated from the top flight for the first time in 1920, and did not return until 1926, and in the <a href="/wiki/1927%E2%80%9328_in_English_football" title="1927–28 in English football">1927–28</a> season they looked like going down again before securing a haul of 17 points from their last 10 matches to secure safety. Wednesday went on to win the League title the following season (<a href="/wiki/1928%E2%80%9329_in_English_football" title="1928–29 in English football">1928–29</a>), which started a run that saw the team finishing lower than third only once until 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-Football_in_Sheffield_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Football_in_Sheffield-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The period was topped off with the team winning the FA Cup for the third time in the club's history in <a href="/wiki/1935_FA_Cup_Final" title="1935 FA Cup Final">1935</a>. When <a href="/wiki/World_War_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="World War Two">World War Two</a> began, the club entered non-competitive war leagues, returning to the status quo in 1946.
</p>
<h3><span id="The_yo-yo_years_.281945.E2.80.931989.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_yo-yo_years_(1945–1989)">The yo-yo years (1945–1989)</span></h3>
<p>The 1950s saw Wednesday unable to consistently hold on to a position in the top flight and this period became known as the <a href="/wiki/Yo-yo_club" title="Yo-yo club">yo-yo years</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bullock_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullock-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> After being promoted in 1950 they were relegated three times, although each time they returned to the top flight by winning the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> the following season. The decade ended on a high note with the team finishing in the top half of the First Division for the first time since the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.
</p><p>In 1961, the club ran toe-to-toe with <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> at the top of the table for the majority of the season – Wednesday became the first team to beat Spurs all season – before finally finishing in second place, which still (as of 2019) remains the club's highest post-war league finish. In 1966 the club reached its fifth FA Cup final, but they were beaten 2–3 by Everton, having led 2–0.
</p><p>Off the field the club was embroiled in the <a href="/wiki/British_betting_scandal_of_1964" class="mw-redirect" title="British betting scandal of 1964">British betting scandal of 1964</a> in which three of its players, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Swan_(footballer_born_1936)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Swan (footballer born 1936)">Peter Swan</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Layne" title="David Layne">David Layne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Kay" title="Tony Kay">Tony Kay</a>, were accused of <a href="/wiki/Match_fixing" title="Match fixing">match fixing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sports_betting" title="Sports betting">betting</a> against their own team in an away game at <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a>. The three were subsequently convicted and, on release from prison, banned from football for life.<sup id="cite_ref-Betting_Scandal_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Betting_Scandal-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The three were reprieved in the early 1970s, with Swan and Layne returning to Hillsborough, and, though their careers were virtually over, Swan at least played some league games for The Owls.
</p><p>Wednesday were relegated at the end of the <a href="/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_in_English_football" title="1969–70 in English football">1969–70 season</a>; this began the darkest period in the club's history, eventually culminating in the club dropping to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> for the first time in its history, and in 1976 it almost fell into the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Fourth_Division" title="Football League Fourth Division">Fourth Division</a>. It was not until the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Charlton" title="Jack Charlton">Jack Charlton</a> as manager in 1977 that the club started to climb back up the league pyramid. Charlton led the Owls back to the Second Division in 1980 before handing the reins to <a href="/wiki/Howard_Wilkinson" title="Howard Wilkinson">Howard Wilkinson</a>, who took the club back into the top flight in 1984, after an absence of 14 years.
</p><p>On 15 April 1989 the club's stadium was the scene of <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_disaster" title="Hillsborough disaster">one of the worst sporting tragedies ever</a>, at the FA Cup semi-final between <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a>, at which 96 Liverpool fans were fatally crushed in the Leppings Lane end of the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The tragedy resulted in many changes at Hillsborough and all other leading stadiums in England; it was required that all capacity should be of seats rather than of terracing for fans to stand,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and that perimeter fencing should be removed.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Life_at_the_top_of_the_Premier_League_.281989.E2.80.931995.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_at_the_top_of_the_Premier_League_(1989–1995)">Life at the top of the Premier League (1989–1995)</span></h3>
<p>In Atkinson's first full season as manager, 1989–90, Sheffield Wednesday finished 18th in the First Division and were relegated on <a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">goal difference</a>, despite the acquisition of the talented <a href="/wiki/John_Sheridan_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Sheridan (football)">John Sheridan</a> and the fact they had pulled towards mid-table at one stage of the season. They regained promotion at the first attempt but the real highlight of the season was a League Cup final victory over Atkinson's old club Manchester United. <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">Midfielder</a> Sheridan scored the only goal of the game, which delivered the club's first major trophy since their FA Cup success of 1935. Atkinson moved to <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> shortly after promotion was achieved, and handed over the reins to 37-year-old striker <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a>.
</p><p>Wednesday finished third in the First Division at the end of the 1991–92 season, booking their place in the following season's UEFA Cup and becoming a founder member of the new <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League">FA Premier League</a>.
</p><p>1992–93 was one of the most eventful seasons in the history of Sheffield Wednesday football club. They finished seventh in the Premier League and reached the finals of both the FA Cup and the League Cup, but were on the losing side to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in both games, the FA Cup final going to a replay and only settled in the last minute of extra time. This prevented the Owls from making another appearance in European competition. Still, the 1992–93 season established Sheffield Wednesday as a top club. <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">Midfielder</a> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Waddle" title="Chris Waddle">Chris Waddle</a> was voted <a href="/wiki/Football_Writers%27_Association_Footballer_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Writers&#39; Association Footballer of the Year">Football Writers' Association Footballer of the Year</a>, and the strike partnership of <a href="/wiki/David_Hirst_(footballer)" title="David Hirst (footballer)">David Hirst</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bright" title="Mark Bright">Mark Bright</a> was one of the most feared in the country. Francis was unable to achieve any more success at the club, and two seasons later he was sacked. His successor was former <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham</a> manager <a href="/wiki/David_Pleat" title="David Pleat">David Pleat</a>.
</p><p>David Pleat's first season as Sheffield Wednesday manager was frustrating, as they finished 15th in the Premiership despite an expensively-assembled line-up which included the likes of <a href="/wiki/Marc_Degryse" title="Marc Degryse">Marc Degryse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Stefanovic" class="mw-redirect" title="Dejan Stefanovic">Dejan Stefanovic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darko_Kovacevic" class="mw-redirect" title="Darko Kovacevic">Darko Kovacevic</a> – who all had disappointing and short-lived tenures at the club. An excellent start to the 1996–97 season saw the Owls top the Premiership after winning their first four games, and David Pleat was credited <a href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League_Manager_of_the_Month" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Premier League Manager of the Month">Manager of the Month</a> for August 1996. But the club failed to mount a serious title challenge and they faded away to finish seventh in the final table. Pleat was sacked the following November with the club struggling at the wrong end of the Premiership, and Ron Atkinson briefly returned to steer the Owls clear of relegation.
</p><p>At the end of the 1997–98 season, Ron Atkinson's short-term contract was not renewed and Sheffield Wednesday turned to the <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> boss <a href="/wiki/Danny_Wilson_(footballer,_born_1960)" title="Danny Wilson (footballer, born 1960)">Danny Wilson</a> as their new manager after being given the backword by both <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Houllier" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerard Houllier">Gerard Houllier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Smith" title="Walter Smith">Walter Smith</a> who joined <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> respectively. Wilson's first season at the helm brought a slight improvement as they finished 12th in the Premiership. An expensively assembled squad including <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Di_Canio" title="Paolo Di Canio">Paolo Di Canio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Carbone" title="Benito Carbone">Benito Carbone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wim_Jonk" title="Wim Jonk">Wim Jonk</a> failed to live up to the massive wage bill the club was paying and things eventually came to a head when Italian firebrand Di Canio was sent off in a match against Arsenal and proceeded to push the referee on his way off. Danny Wilson was sacked the following March with relegation looking a certainty for the Hillsborough club, following a disastrous season where they had been hammered 8–0 by <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> as early as September. His assistant <a href="/wiki/Peter_Shreeves" title="Peter Shreeves">Peter Shreeves</a> took temporary charge but was unable to stave off relegation.
</p>
<h3><span id="Modern_highs_and_lows_.281995.E2.80.932012.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_highs_and_lows_(1995–2012)">Modern highs and lows (1995–2012)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg/220px-Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg/330px-Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg/440px-Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1361" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_SheffieldWednesday2000a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Owls playing in their final away match of the <a href="/wiki/1999-2000_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="1999-2000 Premier League">1999-2000 Premier League</a> season, at Arsenal in May 2000</div></div></div>
<p>Wednesday couldn't keep the forward momentum going however, and by the turn of the new millennium again found itself on the brink of relegation – a 3–3 draw at Arsenal in May 2000 was enough to see the Owls tumble into the First Division. Having spent large sums building squads that were ultimately ineffective, the club's finances took a turn for the worse, and in 2003 they were relegated for a second time in four years, to the Second Division.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_fanzine_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_fanzine-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The club spent two years in the third tier before returning the Championship, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Sturrock" title="Paul Sturrock">Paul Sturrock</a>'s side winning promotion via the play-offs in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-promotion_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-promotion-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Ultimately however, the club's perilous financial position ensured another drop to League 1 was not too far away – five years after the play-off win of 2005, the Owls were again relegated to League 1.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between July and November 2010, Sheffield Wednesday faced a series of <a href="/wiki/Liquidation" title="Liquidation">winding up</a> orders for unpaid tax and <a href="/wiki/VAT" class="mw-redirect" title="VAT">VAT</a> bills, with the club's existence under severe threat.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It was not until 29 November 2010, when businessman <a href="/wiki/Milan_Mandari%C4%87" title="Milan Mandarić">Milan Mandarić</a> agreed to buy out the old owners, that the club could move forward.
</p>
<h3><span id="Fight_back_to_the_top_.282012.E2.80.93Present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_back_to_the_top_(2012–Present)">Fight back to the top (2012–Present)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg/220px-Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg/330px-Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg/440px-Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_Wednesday_Pitch_invasion_5th_May_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wednesday supporters celebrating on the pitch, following promotion to <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">The Championship</a>, on 5 May 2012</div></div></div>
<p>Mandarić appointed former Wednesday player <a href="/wiki/Gary_Megson" title="Gary Megson">Gary Megson</a> as manager partway through the 2010–11 season, and while Megson only stayed in the job for a year, what was mostly his side won promotion back to the Championship in May 2012, under the stewardship of new manager <a href="/wiki/Dave_Jones_(footballer_born_1956)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dave Jones (footballer born 1956)">Dave Jones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014 the club was again taken over by a new owner, Thai businessman <a href="/wiki/Dejphon_Chansiri" title="Dejphon Chansiri">Dejphon Chansiri</a>, purchasing the club from Milan Mandarić for £37.5m.<sup id="cite_ref-dej_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dej-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Chansiri stated his intention to win promotion back to the club for the 2017–18 season – the football club's 150th anniversary – and came close to achieving that goal a year head of schedule, with new coach <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Carvalhal" title="Carlos Carvalhal">Carlos Carvalhal</a> leading the club into the end of season play-offs at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_in_English_football" title="2015–16 in English football">2015–16 season</a>. Wednesday were beaten in the final by <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley" title="Wembley">Wembley</a>. They made the play-offs again the following season, but lost on penalties to the eventually promoted <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Town">Huddersfield Town</a> in the semi final.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The club were favorites to be promoted in the 2017/18 season, but injuries and poor results saw them drop to the lower half of the table. Carvalhal left by mutual consent in December 2017, and was replaced by Dutch manager <a href="/wiki/Jos_Luhukay" title="Jos Luhukay">Jos Luhukay</a> a month later.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The team finished in an uneventful 15th place at the end of the season. Luhukay was sacked in December 2018 after a run of only 1 win in 10, which left the team 18th in the table.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He was replaced by former <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa" class="mw-redirect" title="Aston Villa">Aston Villa</a> boss <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bruce" title="Steve Bruce">Steve Bruce</a> who saw an upturn in form to finish 12th. However, Bruce controversially resigned in July 2019 to manage <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle United">Newcastle United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 September 2019, the club appointed former Birmingham City manager <a href="/wiki/Garry_Monk" title="Garry Monk">Garry Monk</a> as the new manager.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Nickname.2C_kits.2C_crest_and_traditions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname,_kits,_crest_and_traditions">Nickname, kits, crest and traditions</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname">Nickname</span></h3>
<p>In their early years, the club was nicknamed The Blades, a term used for any sporting team from the city of Sheffield, famous the world over for its cutlery and knives. That nickname has been retained by Wednesday's crosstown rivals, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield United">Sheffield United</a>.
</p><p>Although it is widely assumed that the club's nickname changed to The Owls in 1899 after the club's move to Owlerton, it was not until 1912, when Wednesday player <a href="/wiki/George_Robertson_(footballer,_born_1885)" title="George Robertson (footballer, born 1885)">George Robertson</a> presented the club with an <a href="/wiki/Owl" title="Owl">owl</a> mascot, that the name took hold. A monkey mascot introduced some years earlier had not brought much luck.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kits">Kits</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:120px;"><div style="width: 100px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;">
<div style="position: relative; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 100px; height: 135px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;">
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px; background-color: #FFFFFF;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Kit_left_arm_thinnavyhoops.png" decoding="async" title="Team colours" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kit_left_arm.svg/31px-Kit_left_arm.svg.png" decoding="async" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kit_left_arm.svg/47px-Kit_left_arm.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Kit_left_arm.svg/62px-Kit_left_arm.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 31px; top: 0px; width: 38px; height: 59px; background-color: #FFFFFF;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Kit_body_thinnavyhoops.png" decoding="async" width="38" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="38" data-file-height="59" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 31px; top: 0px; width: 38px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kit_body.svg/38px-Kit_body.svg.png" decoding="async" width="38" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kit_body.svg/57px-Kit_body.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kit_body.svg/76px-Kit_body.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="38" data-file-height="59" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 69px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px; background-color: #FFFFFF;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Kit_right_arm_thinnavyhoops.png" decoding="async" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 69px; top: 0px; width: 31px; height: 59px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/31px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png" decoding="async" width="31" height="59" style="vertical-align: top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/47px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Kit_right_arm.svg/62px-Kit_right_arm.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="31" data-file-height="59" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 36px; background-color: #FFFFFF"></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 36px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/100px-Kit_shorts.svg.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="36" style="vertical-align: top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/150px-Kit_shorts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/200px-Kit_shorts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="36" /></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 95px; width: 100px; height: 40px; background-color: #FFFFFF"></div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 95px; width: 100px; height: 40px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Kit_socks_long.svg/100px-Kit_socks_long.svg.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="40" style="vertical-align: top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Kit_socks_long.svg/150px-Kit_socks_long.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Kit_socks_long.svg/200px-Kit_socks_long.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="100" data-file-height="40" /></div>
</div>
</div></div><div class="thumbcaption">The Wednesday's home shirt of 1871. It is assumed that these were the original colours used by the team.</div></div></div>
<p>Since its founding the club has played their home games in blue and white shirts, traditionally in vertical stripes. However, this has not always been the case and there have been variations upon the theme. A monochrome photograph from 1874–75 shows the Wednesday team in plain dark shirts,<sup id="cite_ref-Romance_of_the_Wednesday_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romance_of_the_Wednesday-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> while the 1871 "Rules of the Sheffield Football Association" listed the Wednesday club colours as blue and white hoops.<sup id="cite_ref-Football_in_Sheffield_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Football_in_Sheffield-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> A quartered blue and white design was used in 1887 and a blue shirt with white sleeves between 1965 and 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-Club_Colours_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Club_Colours-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Wednesday's socks have been predominantly black, blue or white throughout their history.
</p><p>The club's away strip has changed regularly over the years. Traditionally, white was the second choice for many teams, including Wednesday, although the club has used a multitude of colours for its change strip over the years, including yellow, black, silver, green and orange.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crest">Crest</span></h3>
<p>Since 1912, the owl has become a theme that has run throughout the club. The original club crest was introduced in 1956<sup id="cite_ref-crest_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crest-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and consisted of a shield showing a traditionally drawn owl perched on a branch. The <a href="/wiki/White_Rose_of_York" title="White Rose of York">White Rose of York</a><sup id="cite_ref-olderbadge_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olderbadge-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> was depicted below the branch alluding to the home county of <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a> and the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sheaf" class="extiw" title="wikt:sheaf">sheaves</a> of Sheffield <i>(Sheaf field)</i> were shown at either side of the owl's head. The club's <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> motto, <i>Consilio et Animis</i>, was displayed beneath the shield.<sup id="cite_ref-crest_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crest-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> This translates into English as "<i>By Wisdom and Courage</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-motto_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motto-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The crest was changed in 1970 to a minimalist version designed by a local art student, and this logo was used by the club, with variations, until 1995, when it was replaced by a similar design to the original crest. It again featured a traditionally drawn owl perched on a branch although the design of both had changed. The sheaves were replaced by a stylised <i>SWFC</i> logo that had been in use on club merchandise for several years prior to the introduction of the new crest. The <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Rose" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Rose">Yorkshire Rose</a> was moved to above the owl's head to make way for the words <i>Sheffield Wednesday</i>. The word <i>Hillsborough</i> was also curved around the top of the design. The club motto was absent on the new design. The crest was encased in a new shape of shield. This crest remained in use for only a few years, during which several versions were used with different colours, including a white crest with blue stripes down either side and the colouring of the detail inverted.<sup id="cite_ref-badge_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-badge-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1999, the minimalist version was brought back, albeit inside a crest, and with the addition of a <a href="/wiki/Copyright_symbol" title="Copyright symbol">copyright symbol</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-crest_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crest-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, new owner Dejphon Chansiri again changed the club crest, opting for a similar design to the 1956 badge.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

		</div></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascots">Mascots</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ozzieowl.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ozzieowl.jpg/220px-Ozzieowl.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ozzieowl.jpg/330px-Ozzieowl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ozzieowl.jpg/440px-Ozzieowl.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ozzieowl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ozzie Owl, the primary club mascot</div></div></div>
<p>Over the years Sheffield Wednesday have had several <a href="/wiki/Owl" title="Owl">Owl</a> themed matchday <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascots</a>. Originally it was Ozzie the Owl and later two further Owls, Baz &amp; Ollie were added. All three were replaced in 2006 by Barney Owl, a similar looking owl but with more defined eyes to make it look cuter. Ozzie Owl was reintroduced as Wednesday's main mascot during the home game with Charlton Athletic on 17 January 2009. The current mascots are Ozzie and Barney Owl. In 2012, Ollie Owl also made his return to the scene, as the club announced him Mascot for the Owls work with children in the local community.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_stadiums">Past stadiums</span></h3>
<p>Originally, Wednesday played matches at <a href="/wiki/Highfield_(stadium)" title="Highfield (stadium)">Highfield</a>, but moved several times before adopting a permanent ground. Other locations included <a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Road" title="Myrtle Road">Myrtle Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heeley" title="Heeley">Heeley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hunter%27s_Bar" title="Hunter&#39;s Bar">Hunter's Bar</a>. Major matches were played at <a href="/wiki/Sheaf_House" title="Sheaf House">Sheaf House</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>, before <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> made it their home ground.<sup id="cite_ref-Wednesday!_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wednesday!-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield Wednesday's first permanent home ground was at <a href="/wiki/Olive_Grove" title="Olive Grove">Olive Grove</a>, a site near Queen's Road originally leased from the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Fitzalan-Howard,_15th_Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Henry Fitzalan-Howard, 15th Duke of Norfolk">Duke of Norfolk</a>. The first game at Olive Grove was a 4–4 draw with <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> on 12 September 1887. Extensions to the adjacent railway forced the club to move to their current ground in 1899.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hillsborough_Stadium">Hillsborough Stadium</span></h3>
<p>Since 1899 Wednesday have played their home games at <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough Stadium</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Owlerton" title="Owlerton">Owlerton</a> district of Sheffield. The stadium was originally named Owlerton Stadium but in 1914 Owlerton became part of the parliamentary constituency of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Hillsborough_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Sheffield Hillsborough (UK Parliament constituency)">Hillsborough</a> and the ground took on its current name.<sup id="cite_ref-About_Hillsborough_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Hillsborough-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> With 39,732 seats, Hillsborough has the third highest capacity of stadiums in <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_stadiums_in_England" title="List of stadiums in England">12th highest</a> in England. The club intended to increase Hillsborough's capacity to 44,825 by 2012 and 50,000 by 2016 and make several other improvements in the process, but due to England's failed World Cup bid, this is now not the case.<sup id="cite_ref-swfc_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swfc-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The stadium has hosted <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> football (1966), The 1996 European Championships (<a href="/wiki/Euro_96" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 96">Euro 96</a>) and 27 FA Cup Semi-finals. The Kop at Hillsborough was re-opened in 1986 by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and was once the largest covered stand of any football stadium in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 April 1989 at an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final between <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a>, 96 Liverpool fans were crushed to death after the terraces at the Leppings Lane end of the ground became overcrowded, in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_disaster" title="Hillsborough disaster">Hillsborough disaster</a>. The following report concluded that the root cause of the disaster was the failure of local police to adequately manage the crowds.<sup id="cite_ref-Hillsborough_justice_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillsborough_justice-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hillsborough_HSE_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillsborough_HSE-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> A memorial to the victims of the disaster stands outside Hillsborough's South Stand, near the main entrance on Parkside Road. After many years of dispute about the facts, in June 2017 six men responsible for safety were charged with criminal offences including manslaughter and misconduct in public office.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:908px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillsborough_Stadium,_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2024092.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Hillsborough Stadium in 2009"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Hillsborough_Stadium%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2024092.jpg/900px-Hillsborough_Stadium%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2024092.jpg" decoding="async" width="900" height="289" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Hillsborough_Stadium%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2024092.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="329" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hillsborough_Stadium,_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2024092.jpg" title="File:Hillsborough Stadium, Sheffield - geograph.org.uk - 2024092.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of Hillsborough Stadium in 2009</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg/220px-SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg/330px-SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg/440px-SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SheffieldWednesdayFans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wednesday fans at Hillsborough in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>The club's move to Owlerton in 1899 was a risky one as it moved the club several miles away from the city centre, but the loyal followers continued to make the journey to the new ground and the club has been one of the best supported in England ever since, although official attendances weren't taken at Football League games until the 1920s.
</p><p>The club's highest average attendance over the course of a season was 42,530 in 1952–53, when gates across the country were at their highest. The lowest average attendance in the Owls' history came in 1978–79, when an average of just 10,643 fans turned out to watch their side.
</p><p>In 1992 Wednesday were the fourth best supported team in the country, but although that ranking has come down since relegation from the Premier League in 2000, the club still has still enjoyed crowds of well over 20,000 since then, and was the best supported club outside the top flight in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-2005–2006_Attendances_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005–2006_Attendances-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2003-2004_Division_2_Attendances_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2003-2004_Division_2_Attendances-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2004-2005_League_1_Attendances_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004-2005_League_1_Attendances-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 2005 playoff final, Wednesday took over 39,000 fans to the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sturrock_salutes_fans_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sturrock_salutes_fans-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Sheffield Wednesday took over 38,000 fans to Wembley for a play-off final defeat by Hull City, selling substantially more seats than their counterparts many of whom boycotted the game.
The Owls have managed to average 30000 at home in the last 60 years. The FA Cup Final seasons in 1965/6 30000 and 1966/7 31000 plus 32000 when coming League Championship Runners Up in 1960/61.
</p><p>Sheffield Wednesday have had a large variety of fanzines over the years; examples include <i>Just Another Wednesday</i>, <i>Out of the Blue</i>, <i>Spitting Feathers</i>, <i>Boddle</i>, <i>A View From The East Bank</i>, <i>Cheat!</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Monster_Trucks" title="War of the Monster Trucks">War of the Monster Trucks</a></i>, which acquired its name from the programme that <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Television">Yorkshire Television</a> elected to show instead of the celebrations after the <a href="/wiki/1991_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1991 Football League Cup Final">1991 League Cup</a> victory over Manchester United.<sup id="cite_ref-About_WOTMT_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_WOTMT-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several online message boards dedicated to discussions on the club, including Owlstalk, OwlsOnline and OwlsMad.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry">Rivalry</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WednesdayUnited2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/WednesdayUnited2012.jpg/220px-WednesdayUnited2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/WednesdayUnited2012.jpg/330px-WednesdayUnited2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/WednesdayUnited2012.jpg/440px-WednesdayUnited2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WednesdayUnited2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wednesday vs United just before the 2012 league fixture at Hillsborough. Wednesday won 1–0 and went on to pip their rivals to promotion</div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield Wednesday's main rivals are city neighbours <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>. Matches between these two clubs are nicknamed <a href="/wiki/Steel_City_derby" title="Steel City derby">Steel City derbies</a>, so called because of the steel industry the city of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a> is famous for.
</p><p>United were formed in 1889 by the committee at <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>, who had lost their biggest source of income – Wednesday – two years earlier over a dispute concerning pitch rent. As well as playing at Wednesday's former ground, United also took Wednesday's former nickname, the Blades, as their own. The first derby game took place on 15 December 1890, with Wednesday winning 2–1 at <a href="/wiki/Olive_Grove" title="Olive Grove">Olive Grove</a>.
</p><p>The 1993 <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final match which took place at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley</a> on 3 April 1993. Initially, it was announced that the match was scheduled to take place at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> but this was met with dismay by both sets of fans. After a re-think, <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a> decided to switch venue to Wembley. A crowd of 75,365 supporters made the trip down to London to watch Wednesday beat United 2–1 after extra time in a match which Wednesday dominated heavily.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C._records" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C. records">Sheffield Wednesday F.C. records</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg/220px-SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="81" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg/330px-SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg/440px-SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SheffieldWednesdayFC_League_Performance.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Historical league position since 1892–93</div></div></div>
<p>Wednesday's biggest recorded win was a 12–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Halliwell_F.C." title="Halliwell F.C.">Halliwell</a> in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> on 18 January 1891. The biggest league win was against <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Division 1</a> on 13 December 1930; Wednesday won 9–1. Both of these wins occurred at home.
</p><p>The heaviest defeat was away from home against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> in a Division 1 match on 5 October 1912 which Wednesday lost 10–0.
</p><p>The most goals scored by the club in a season was the 106 scored in the <a href="/wiki/1958%E2%80%9359_in_English_football" title="1958–59 in English football">1958–59 season</a>. The club accumulated their highest league points total in the 2011–12 season when they racked up 93 points.
</p><p>The highest home attendance was in the FA Cup fifth round on 17 February 1934. A total of 72,841 turned up to see a 2–2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>. Unfortunately for Wednesday, they went on to lose the replay 2–0. Manchester City won the FA Cup that season.
</p><p>The most <a href="/wiki/Cap_(sport)" title="Cap (sport)">capped</a> Englishman to play for the club was goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Ron_Springett" title="Ron Springett">Ron Springett</a> who won 33 caps while at Sheffield Wednesday. Springett also held the overall record for most capped Sheffield Wednesday player until <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Worthington" title="Nigel Worthington">Nigel Worthington</a> broke the record, eventually gaining a total of 50 caps for <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Northern Ireland</a> whilst at the club.
</p><p>The fastest sending off in British league football is held by Sheffield Wednesday goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Pressman" title="Kevin Pressman">Kevin Pressman</a> – who was sent off after just 13 seconds for handling a shot from Wolverhampton's <a href="/wiki/Temuri_Ketsbaia" class="mw-redirect" title="Temuri Ketsbaia">Temuri Ketsbaia</a> outside the area during the opening weekend of 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-fastest_send-lff_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastest_send-lff-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The fastest shot ever recorded in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> was hit by David Hirst against Arsenal at Highbury in September 1996 – Hirst hit the bar with a shot clocked at 114 <a href="/wiki/Miles_per_hour" title="Miles per hour">mph</a>.
</p>

<p>Dickinson, who was in charge for 29 years, is Wednesday's longest-serving manager, and helped establish the club during the first two decades of the 20th century.
</p><p>Brown succeeded Dickinson and remained in charge for 13 years; in 1930 he secured their most recent top division league title to date.
</p><p>Taylor took over during the Second World War and remained in charge until 1958, but failed to win a major trophy, even though Wednesday were in the top flight for most of his reign.
</p><p>Charlton took Wednesday out of the Third Division in 1980 and in his final season (<a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_in_English_football" title="1982–83 in English football">1982–83</a>) he took them to the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>.
</p><p>Wilkinson succeeded Charlton in the summer of 1983 and was in charge for more than five years before he moved to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_A.F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds United A.F.C.">Leeds United</a>. His first season saw Wednesday gain promotion to the First Division after a 14-year exile. He guided them to a fifth-place finish in 1986, but Wednesday were unable to compete in the 1986–87 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> due to the ban on English teams in European competitions due to the <a href="/wiki/Heysel_Disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Heysel Disaster">Heysel Disaster</a> of 1985.
</p><p>Francis took over as player-manager in June 1991 after <a href="/wiki/Ron_Atkinson" title="Ron Atkinson">Ron Atkinson</a> (who had just guided them to <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">Football League Cup</a> glory and promotion to the First Division) departed to <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>. He guided them to third place in the league in 1992, and earned them a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> place. They finished seventh in the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_in_English_football" title="1992–93 in English football">inaugural</a> <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> and were runners-up of the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> and League Cup that year. He was sacked in 1995 after Wednesday finished 13th – their lowest standing in four years since winning promotion.
</p>
